     1	# Karpathy LLM Wiki Strategy for Orbital Inspect
     2	
     3	Date: April 18, 2026
     4	
     5	## Executive Summary
     6	
     7	Orbital Inspect already has a strong raw-evidence and audit substrate:
     8	
     9	- canonical assets, aliases, and reference profiles in `backend/db/models.py`
    10	- reusable evidence records and analysis-evidence lineage in `backend/db/models.py` and `backend/db/repository.py`
    11	- persisted analysis events, decision workflow, governance, reports, fleet trends, and offline eval hooks across `backend/main.py` and `backend/services/`
    12	
    13	What it does not yet have is the layer Andrej Karpathy is now implicitly optimizing for: a compiled, persistent, queryable knowledge layer that sits between raw evidence and each new reasoning run.
    14	
    15	My judgment:
    16	
    17	- Karpathy's April 4, 2026 `llm-wiki` idea file is directly relevant to Orbital Inspect.
    18	- Rohit Ghumare's April 18, 2026 `LLM Wiki v2` gist is useful, but only after translation into Orbital Inspect's stricter provenance, governance, and multi-tenant requirements.
    19	- The right move is not "add an Obsidian clone."
    20	- The right move is to turn Orbital Inspect from an evidence-rich analysis system into an evidence-rich analysis system with compiled institutional memory.
    21	
    22	That means:
    23	
    24	1. keep raw evidence as source of truth
    25	2. compile claims, precedents, and workflows into a durable knowledge layer
    26	3. use that layer for context engineering, human review, and fleet intelligence
    27	4. never allow unreviewed compiled knowledge to bypass fail-closed underwriting logic
    28	
    29	## Source Grounding
    30	
    31	The latest directly inspectable long-form source from Andrej Karpathy I found is his `llm-wiki` gist, created on April 4, 2026:
    32	
    33	- https://gist.github.com/karpathy/442a6bf555914893e9891c11519de94f
    34	
    35	Two earlier Karpathy signals still matter because they explain how to use the wiki pattern correctly:
    36	
    37	- June 19, 2025: `Andrej Karpathy: Software Is Changing (Again)` at YC AI Startup School
    38	  - https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=LCEmiRjPEtQ
    39	- June 25, 2025: Karpathy's `context engineering` post, which defines the real systems problem as packing the context window with the right information for the next step
    40	  - surfaced in Techmeme: https://www.techmeme.com/250628/h1150
    41	
    42	The user-linked extension gist is:
    43	
    44	- April 18, 2026: Rohit Ghumare, `LLM Wiki v2`
    45	  - https://gist.github.com/rohitg00/2067ab416f7bbe447c1977edaaa681e2
    46	
    47	Important dating point: as of April 18, 2026, I did not find a newer directly inspectable Karpathy long-form source than the April 4, 2026 gist. The repo plan below is therefore grounded primarily in that gist, plus his June 2025 context-engineering and Software 3.0 framing.
    48	
    49	Everything below that maps those sources into Orbital Inspect is my inference, not a claim that Karpathy explicitly prescribed this exact architecture for this repo.
    50	
    51	## What Karpathy Is Actually Saying
    52	
    53	### 1. Stop re-deriving; start compiling
    54	
    55	Karpathy's core complaint with standard RAG is not that retrieval is useless. It is that the system keeps rediscovering the same knowledge from raw documents every time. His proposed fix is a persistent wiki maintained by the LLM, where synthesis accumulates.
    56	
    57	For Orbital Inspect, this is the key leap:
    58	
    59	- today: every new analysis reassembles evidence, prior analyses, reference profiles, and stage outputs mostly per run
    60	- target: the system should also maintain compiled knowledge about assets, subsystems, anomalies, failure signatures, operator patterns, and precedent cases
    61	
    62	### 2. The schema is the product
    63	
    64	Karpathy's architecture has three layers:
    65	
    66	- raw sources
    67	- wiki
    68	- schema
    69	
    70	Orbital Inspect already has strong raw sources. It partially has a schema through `AGENTS.md`, service boundaries, prompt files, and governance policy. It does not yet have the middle compiled-knowledge layer in a first-class form.
    71	
    72	This matters because Orbital Inspect is not a toy coding-agent workspace. It is an insurance and operational-intelligence system. The schema has to encode:
    73	
    74	- what counts as a claim
    75	- what counts as a precedent
    76	- what can influence runtime decisions
    77	- what requires human validation
    78	- how confidence changes with recency and contradiction
    79	- what is tenant-scoped, global, classified, or non-exportable
    80	
    81	### 3. Context engineering beats prompt engineering
    82	
    83	Karpathy's June 25, 2025 observation is the most operationally important one for this repo: the problem is not clever prompts, it is assembling the right context for the next step.
    84	
    85	Orbital Inspect is already a context-heavy system:
    86	
    87	- the 5-agent pipeline
    88	- evidence bundles
    89	- reference profiles
    90	- historical analyses
    91	- fleet trends
    92	- governance and human review state
    93	
    94	The next level is to make this context compiled and selective rather than merely available.
    95	
    96	### 4. Partial autonomy beats blind autonomy
    97	
    98	From Karpathy's Software 3.0 framing, the winning application shape is not "turn the human off." It is "push autonomy up where it compounds, keep the human where risk concentrates."
    99	
   100	Orbital Inspect already follows this principle well:
   101	
   102	- fail-closed outputs
   103	- `FURTHER_INVESTIGATION` escalation
   104	- human review requirements
   105	- governance holds
   106	
   107	The wiki strategy should strengthen that pattern, not weaken it.
   108	
   109	### 5. The human should curate; the system should maintain
   110	
   111	Karpathy's core product insight is that humans abandon knowledge bases because maintenance is annoying. The LLM should do the bookkeeping.
   112	
   113	For Orbital Inspect, the bookkeeping burden is not just notes. It is:
   114	
   115	- cross-case precedent maintenance
   116	- contradiction tracking across evidence sources
   117	- subsystem-specific anomaly pattern extraction
   118	- prompt and policy drift tracking
   119	- keeping asset baseline knowledge current as new public and internal evidence arrives
   120	
   121	## What Rohit's LLM Wiki v2 Adds
   122	
   123	Rohit's gist is useful because it extends Karpathy's intentionally abstract pattern into production concerns. The strongest additions are:
   124	
   125	### 1. Memory lifecycle
   126	
   127	This is the most important extension.
   128	
   129	The gist adds:
   130	
   131	- confidence scoring
   132	- supersession
   133	- forgetting and retention curves
   134	- consolidation tiers from working memory to procedural memory
   135	
   136	This maps extremely well to Orbital Inspect because your data already has strong provenance and time semantics. The missing piece is not storage; it is lifecycle.
   137	
   138	### 2. Typed graph structure
   139	
   140	The shift from flat pages to entities and typed relationships is exactly right for orbital intelligence.
   141	
   142	Relevant entity classes for this repo would include:
   143	
   144	- asset
   145	- subsystem
   146	- orbit regime
   147	- anomaly
   148	- evidence source
   149	- failure mechanism
   150	- environmental stressor
   151	- insurance claim pattern
   152	- operator
   153	- precedent case
   154	- mitigation action
   155	
   156	### 3. Hybrid retrieval
   157	
   158	BM25 plus vectors plus graph traversal is directionally right, but not all at once.
   159	
   160	For Orbital Inspect, the ordering should be:
   161	
   162	1. lexical plus structured filters
   163	2. graph traversal over typed entities and relations
   164	3. optional embeddings where semantic recall is genuinely needed
   165	
   166	This repo is audit-heavy and domain-bounded. Over-indexing on embeddings too early would create opaque behavior without enough gain.
   167	
   168	### 4. Automation hooks
   169	
   170	The gist's event-driven mindset is highly compatible with this codebase:
   171	
   172	- on new evidence ingest
   173	- on completed analysis
   174	- on decision review completion
   175	- on scheduled fleet refresh
   176	- on contradiction detection
   177	- on benchmark failure
   178	
   179	Orbital Inspect already has durable points to hook:
   180	
   181	- `evidence_ingest_service.py`
   182	- `post_analysis_service.py`
   183	- `fleet_ingestion_service.py`
   184	- `retention_service.py`
   185	- `dataset_registry_service.py`
   186	
   187	### 5. Crystallization
   188	
   189	Rohit's "crystallization" idea is excellent for this repo.
   190	
   191	Every finished analysis should not only remain a finished analysis. It should optionally produce:
   192	
   193	- normalized case summary
   194	- extracted claims
   195	- detected anomaly signatures
   196	- precedent links
   197	- lessons for prompt/policy tuning
   198	
   199	This is how the system compounds instead of just storing reports.
   200	
   201	## Where Orbital Inspect Already Has a Head Start
   202	
   203	The repo is closer to a Karpathy-compatible system than it may look.
   204	
   205	### Raw source layer already exists
   206	
   207	Orbital Inspect already stores:
   208	
   209	- reusable evidence records with provider, URL, confidence, capture time, and tags
   210	- reference profiles
   211	- ingest run history
   212	- persisted analysis events
   213	- reports
   214	- baseline references and telemetry summaries on analyses
   215	
   216	That is stronger than most LLM wiki implementations, which start from loose markdown files.
   217	
   218	### Provenance discipline already exists
   219	
   220	`backend/models/provenance.py` already encodes a worldview Karpathy's pattern needs:
   221	
   222	- source types
   223	- field provenance
   224	- confidence calibration
   225	- derivation chains
   226	
   227	This is a major advantage. It means the compiled memory layer can be rigorous rather than vibes-only.
   228	
   229	### Governance discipline already exists
   230	
   231	`backend/services/decision_policy_service.py` and `backend/services/governance_service.py` already enforce:
   232	
   233	- fail-closed logic
   234	- blocked decisions
   235	- explicit human review
   236	- policy-versioned rationale
   237	
   238	That is the right skeleton for safe knowledge compilation.
   239	
   240	### Temporal history already exists
   241	
   242	The repo already thinks in time:
   243	
   244	- captured vs ingested timestamps
   245	- analysis timelines
   246	- trend analysis
   247	- retention policies
   248	- SLO freshness concepts
   249	
   250	This is exactly what a knowledge lifecycle needs.
   251	
   252	## The Critical Insight for Orbital Inspect
   253	
   254	Karpathy's wiki pattern should not be implemented here as a notes feature.
   255	
   256	It should be implemented as a compiled orbital intelligence layer with four jobs:
   257	
   258	1. compress raw evidence into reusable claims and precedents
   259	2. improve context packs for the 5-agent pipeline
   260	3. improve human review speed and consistency

 succeeded in 0ms:
     1	# Orbital Inspect: Autonomous Intelligence Layer
     2	## Integrating Autoresearch + Knowledge Crystallization + Agent Harness
     3	
     4	### Context
     5	
     6	Orbital Inspect has completed Phases 1-2 of the enterprise transformation (API versioning, batch endpoints, fleet-scale ops). The platform is at ~32,664 LOC with a 5-stage AI analysis pipeline. The next evolution: making the system **self-improving** by integrating three paradigms:
     7	
     8	1. **Karpathy's Autoresearch** — Conjecture-test-critique loops that autonomously improve satellite inspection accuracy
     9	2. **LLM Wiki v2 Knowledge Crystallization** (rohitg00 gist) — Confidence-scored facts with typed relationships, consolidation tiers, and hybrid search
    10	3. **OpenClaw-like Agent Harness** — Persistent agent sessions, event-driven triggers, A2A messaging, sandboxed execution
    11	
    12	**Why**: SpaceX doesn't want a tool that inspects satellites — they want a system that **learns from every inspection** and gets smarter over time. The autoresearch loop generates hypotheses, the knowledge layer remembers what works, and the harness orchestrates it all autonomously.
    13	
    14	**Existing integration seams already in place**:
    15	- `additional_context` field (main.py:715) → inject hypotheses into every pipeline agent
    16	- `baseline_reference` JSON (main.py:300-304) → persist winning priors
    17	- `triage_score` (decision_policy_service.py:186-241) → evaluation metric (val_bpb equivalent)
    18	- `DatasetRegistry` (db/models.py:264-292) → SPEED+/OPS-SAT-AD benchmarks for offline eval
    19	- ARQ queue, SSE streaming, webhook dispatch, alert service, fleet ingestion — all reusable
    20	
    21	---
    22	
    23	## Layer 1: Autoresearch Loop Service (Week 1-2)
    24	
    25	**Wow moment**: System autonomously discovers that a satellite's solar array is degrading from atomic oxygen — before a human operator notices.
    26	
    27	### Architecture
    28	
    29	```
    30	Question: "Why is NORAD 25544 showing elevated risk?"
    31	     ↓
    32	CONJECTURE → "Solar array degradation from atomic oxygen exposure"
    33	     ↓
    34	TEST → Run 5-agent pipeline with hypothesis in additional_context
    35	     ↓
    36	EVALUATE → Extract triage_score × evidence_completeness_pct
    37	     ↓
    38	CRITIQUE → LLM evaluates: did hypothesis improve accuracy?
    39	     ↓
    40	ITERATE or PROMOTE → Winning hypothesis → baseline_reference
    41	```
    42	
    43	### Evaluation Metric (val_bpb equivalent)
    44	
    45	```python
    46	composite_metric = triage_score × (evidence_completeness_pct / 100)
    47	# triage_score: 0-1.0 from compute_triage() in decision_policy_service.py:186-241
    48	# evidence_completeness_pct: % of pipeline stages that succeeded
    49	# Lower composite = better (fewer gaps, lower risk misclassification)
    50	```
    51	
    52	### New Files
    53	
    54	| File | Purpose | ~LOC |
    55	|------|---------|------|
    56	| `backend/autoresearch/__init__.py` | Package init | 5 |
    57	| `backend/autoresearch/models.py` | Pydantic: ResearchSession, Hypothesis, ExperimentRun, CritiqueResult | 80 |
    58	| `backend/autoresearch/service.py` | Main conjecture-test-critique loop, adapted from user's Autoresearch/engine/core/engine.py | 200 |
    59	| `backend/autoresearch/evaluator.py` | TriageEvaluator: composite metric extraction from completed analyses | 60 |
    60	| `backend/autoresearch/baseline_promoter.py` | Persists winning hypotheses into baseline_reference + PRIOR_ANALYSIS evidence | 80 |
    61	| `backend/autoresearch/prompts.yaml` | Domain-specific prompts for satellite anomaly conjecture/critique | 60 |
    62	| `backend/autoresearch/tools/__init__.py` | Tool package | 5 |
    63	| `backend/autoresearch/tools/pipeline_tool.py` | Wraps run_satellite_pipeline() with hypothesis injection | 80 |
    64	| `backend/autoresearch/tools/evidence_tool.py` | Queries EvidenceRepository for supporting/contradicting data | 60 |
    65	| `backend/autoresearch/tools/knowledge_tool.py` | Queries Layer 2 knowledge base (wired in Layer 2) | 40 |
    66	| `backend/api/autoresearch.py` | REST endpoints | 100 |
    67	
    68	### Database Schema (Migration 0008)
    69	
    70	**`research_sessions`**: id, org_id, asset_id (FK), dataset_id (FK dataset_registry, NULL=live), status (running/completed/failed/cancelled), question (TEXT), max_iterations (default 10), time_budget_seconds (default 300), current_iteration, best_triage_score, best_hypothesis_id, config_json, created_at, completed_at
    71	
    72	**`research_hypotheses`**: id, session_id (FK), iteration, statement, prediction, confidence (0-1), survived (BOOL), critique_reasoning, triage_score, evidence_completeness_pct, composite_metric, analysis_id (FK analyses), promoted_to_baseline (BOOL), created_at
    73	
    74	### API Endpoints
    75	
    76	```
    77	POST   /api/v1/autoresearch/sessions              -- Start research session
    78	GET    /api/v1/autoresearch/sessions               -- List sessions (org-scoped)
    79	GET    /api/v1/autoresearch/sessions/{id}          -- Detail with hypotheses
    80	GET    /api/v1/autoresearch/sessions/{id}/stream   -- SSE progress
    81	POST   /api/v1/autoresearch/sessions/{id}/cancel   -- Cancel running session
    82	```

   110	---
   111	
   112	## Layer 2: Knowledge Crystallization (Week 2-3)
   113	
   114	**Wow moment**: After analyzing 500 satellites, the system tells SpaceX "satellites on bus platform A3R manufactured before 2019 have a 3.2x higher failure rate in LEO — here's the evidence chain."
   115	
   116	### Architecture
   117	
   118	```
   119	Analysis completes → post_analysis_complete()
   120	     ↓
   121	EXTRACT → Pull facts from each agent's JSON result
   122	     ↓
   123	SCORE → Initial confidence from evidence_completeness_pct
   124	     ↓
   125	MERGE → Bayesian update if similar fact exists (supersession)
   126	     ↓
   127	RELATE → Create typed relationships (caused_by, correlates, contradicts)
   128	     ↓
   129	CONSOLIDATE → Promote through tiers based on evidence accumulation:
   130	  Working (1 analysis) → Episodic (2+ on same asset) → 
   131	  Semantic (3+ assets) → Procedural (used by autoresearch 2+ times)
   132	```
   133	
   134	### Consolidation Tiers (from LLM Wiki v2 gist)
   135	
   136	| Tier | Promotion Criteria | Retention | Example |
   137	|------|-------------------|-----------|---------|
   138	| Working | Auto-created from analysis | 30 days | "ISS solar array shows 12% degradation" |
   139	| Episodic | Confirmed by 2+ analyses on same asset | 90 days | "ISS solar array degradation is progressive" |
   140	| Semantic | Pattern across 3+ assets | 1 year | "LEO satellites show solar array degradation after 5 years" |
   141	| Procedural | Used by autoresearch to improve triage 2+ times | Permanent | "Always check atomic oxygen exposure for LEO solar arrays" |
   142	
   143	### New Files
   144	
   145	| File | Purpose | ~LOC |
   146	|------|---------|------|
   147	| `backend/knowledge/__init__.py` | Package init | 5 |
   148	| `backend/knowledge/models.py` | Pydantic: Fact, Relationship, KnowledgeQuery, SearchResult | 70 |
   149	| `backend/knowledge/ingest_service.py` | Auto-extracts facts from completed analysis results | 150 |
   150	| `backend/knowledge/fact_store.py` | CRUD + confidence scoring + supersession + Bayesian merge | 120 |
   151	| `backend/knowledge/relationship_store.py` | Typed relationship CRUD + graph queries | 80 |
   152	| `backend/knowledge/search_service.py` | BM25 text search + graph traversal + reciprocal rank fusion | 120 |
   153	| `backend/knowledge/consolidation.py` | Tier promotion via periodic ARQ job | 100 |
   154	| `backend/knowledge/pattern_detector.py` | Cross-fleet anomaly correlation | 100 |
   155	| `backend/api/knowledge.py` | REST endpoints | 100 |
   156	
   157	### Database Schema (Migration 0009)
   158	
   159	**`knowledge_facts`**: id, org_id, fact_text (TEXT), fact_type (failure_mode/manufacturer_trait/orbital_regime/anomaly_pattern/inspection_heuristic), domain (solar_array/thermal/attitude_control/propulsion/comms/power), confidence (FLOAT 0-1), tier (working/episodic/semantic/procedural), source_type (analysis/autoresearch/manual/consolidation), source_id, asset_id (FK nullable), superseded_by (self-FK), retention_score (FLOAT), access_count, metadata_json, created_at, updated_at
   160	
   161	**`knowledge_relationships`**: id, org_id, source_fact_id (FK), target_fact_id (FK), relationship_type (uses/depends_on/contradicts/caused/fixed/supersedes/correlates), confidence, evidence_json, created_at. Unique (source, target, type).
   162	
   163	### API Endpoints
   164	
   165	```
   166	GET    /api/v1/knowledge/facts                 -- Search/list facts
   167	GET    /api/v1/knowledge/facts/{id}            -- Fact detail + relationships
   168	GET    /api/v1/knowledge/facts/{id}/related    -- Graph traversal
   169	POST   /api/v1/knowledge/search                -- Hybrid search
   170	GET    /api/v1/knowledge/patterns              -- Fleet-wide pattern summary
   171	GET    /api/v1/knowledge/stats                 -- KB statistics
   172	```
   173

   177	- `backend/config.py` — add KNOWLEDGE_CONSOLIDATION_INTERVAL_HOURS, KNOWLEDGE_RETENTION_DECAY_DAYS (+5 lines)
   178	- `backend/db/models.py` — add KnowledgeFact + KnowledgeRelationship ORM models (+80 lines)
   179	- `backend/db/repository.py` — add KnowledgeRepository class (+100 lines)
   180	- `backend/services/post_analysis_service.py` — call KnowledgeIngestService.ingest_from_analysis() after webhook dispatch (+5 lines)
   181	- `backend/autoresearch/tools/knowledge_tool.py` — wire knowledge search into conjecture generation (+40 lines)
   182	
   183	### Verification
   184	
   185	- [ ] Completing an analysis auto-creates knowledge facts
   186	- [ ] Duplicate facts merge via Bayesian confidence update
   187	- [ ] Search returns relevant facts ranked by fusion score
   188	- [ ] Consolidation promotes facts through tiers based on evidence
   189	- [ ] Pattern detector finds cross-fleet correlations (3+ assets, same failure mode)
   190	- [ ] Knowledge tool feeds patterns into autoresearch conjecture generation
   191	
   192	---
   193	
   194	## Layer 3: Agent Harness (Week 3-5)
   195	
   196	**Wow moment**: New TLE data arrives from CelesTrak at 2am → harness auto-triggers re-analysis → autoresearch detects anomaly → knowledge base updates → Slack alert fires to on-call engineer — zero human intervention.
   197	
   198	### Architecture
   199	
   200	```
   201	EVENT (TLE update / conjunction alert / cron)
   202	     ↓
   203	TRIGGER SERVICE → matches event to registered triggers
   204	     ↓
   205	SESSION MANAGER → creates agent session with memory from previous runs
   206	     ↓
   207	AGENT EXECUTION → pipeline / autoresearch / knowledge consolidation
   208	     ↓
   209	A2A MESSAGING → agents share findings across stages
   210	     ↓
   211	OUTPUT SERVICE → SSE + webhook + Slack + email dispatch
   212	     ↓
   213	SESSION COMPLETE → memory persisted for next activation
   214	```
   215	
   216	### New Files
   217	
   218	| File | Purpose | ~LOC |
   219	|------|---------|------|
   220	| `backend/harness/__init__.py` | Package init | 5 |
   221	| `backend/harness/models.py` | Pydantic: AgentDefinition, AgentSession, Trigger, A2AMessage | 90 |
   222	| `backend/harness/session_manager.py` | Create/resume/suspend/terminate sessions with memory | 120 |
   223	| `backend/harness/trigger_service.py` | Event-driven trigger evaluation + agent activation | 130 |
   224	| `backend/harness/a2a_service.py` | Agent-to-agent message bus (Redis pub/sub + DB persistence) | 120 |
   225	| `backend/harness/sandbox.py` | Execution boundary enforcement (offline eval isolation, org scoping) | 80 |
   226	| `backend/harness/memory_service.py` | Per-agent persistent memory (working state + history) | 90 |
   227	| `backend/harness/output_service.py` | Multi-channel routing (SSE, webhook, Slack, email) | 100 |
   228	| `backend/harness/registry.py` | Agent type registry mapping names → implementations | 60 |
   229	| `backend/harness/wrapped_orchestrator.py` | Harness-aware wrapper around existing orchestrator.py (feature-flagged) | 100 |
   230	| `backend/api/harness.py` | REST endpoints | 120 |
   231	
   232	### Database Schema (Migration 0010)
   233	
   234	**`agent_instances`**: id, org_id, agent_type (classification/vision/environment/failure_mode/insurance_risk/autoresearch/knowledge_consolidation/pattern_detector/fleet_monitor), display_name, config_json, status (idle/running/suspended/terminated), last_active_at, created_at
   235	
   236	**`agent_sessions`**: id, agent_id (FK), org_id, analysis_id (FK nullable), status (active/completed/failed/suspended), started_at, completed_at, execution_time_ms, input_summary (JSON), output_summary (JSON), error_detail
   237	
   238	**`agent_triggers`**: id, org_id, agent_id (FK), trigger_type (data_arrival/alert/cron/a2a_message), trigger_config (JSON), enabled (BOOL), last_fired_at, fire_count, created_at
   239	
   240	**`agent_messages`**: id, org_id, from_agent_id, to_agent_id, message_type (request/response/notification/escalation), payload_json, status (pending/delivered/acknowledged/expired), in_reply_to (self-FK), ttl_seconds (default 3600), created_at, delivered_at
   241	
   242	**`agent_memory`**: id, agent_id (FK), memory_type (working_state/conversation_history/learned_pattern), key, value_json, ttl_seconds, created_at, updated_at. Unique (agent_id, memory_type, key).
   243

   245

   257	GET    /api/v1/harness/messages                -- List A2A messages
   258	```

/bin/bash -lc "nl -ba /tmp/claude-analysis-2026-04-19.md | sed -n '1,320p'" in /mnt/c/Users/kiran/myprojects/orbital-inspect
 succeeded in 0ms:
     1	# Claude Opus 4.7 analysis of KARPATHY_LLM_WIKI_STRATEGY.md
     2	# Date: 2026-04-19
     3	# Target for Codex GPT-5.4 auditor review
     4	
     5	## Verdict in one line each
     6	- Directionally right, one level less principled than it should be.
     7	- Safer than brainstorming/autonomous-intelligence-layer-plan.md, and correctly rejects the features that plan most wants to add.
     8	- Build/measure order is inverted. Eval should precede code, not check it.
     9	- Three first-class invariants are missing: falsifiability, staleness, and cross-source corroboration.
    10	
    11	## 1. Claims that survive hard-to-vary scrutiny (memo is right)
    12	1. The bottleneck is re-derivation, not retrieval. Any system that re-synthesizes the same precedent from raw evidence on every run is paying a synthesis cost whose marginal value trends to zero once paid once correctly. Fixing retrieval does not fix this; only compilation does.
    13	2. Context engineering beats prompt engineering once models are capable enough. Post-2025, marginal returns to prompt tuning collapsed against marginal returns to context quality.
    14	3. Partial autonomy beats blind autonomy in insurance. Underwriting has asymmetric error costs — confident wrong approval is catastrophic, escalation is operational friction. Therefore autonomy must concentrate where error bounds are tight, humans must own the tail.
    15	4. Database-first for canonical claims; markdown for inspection only. Tenant scoping, runtime-eligibility bits, supersession chains, Bayesian merges — markdown-as-truth breaks at any of these.
    16	5. Thin vertical slice before platform. If one agent × one precedent question cannot be measurably improved, five agents × platform will not either.
    17	6. Typed-structure-first retrieval; embeddings last. backend/models/evidence.py and provenance.py already encode a typed world. Vectors before lexical/typed/graph pushes audited systems into opacity.
    18	
    19	## 2. Claims almost-right
    20	1. Case pages as first artifact — correct intuition, missing derivation. My derivation: precedent lookup is inherently 5-dimensional (asset, subsystem, failure_family, operator, orbit_regime). Case page must be keyed on analysis_id with all 5 attributes indexed, not on analysis_id alone.
    21	2. `runtime_eligible: bool` as column — correct concept, wrong mechanism. Governance invariants belong at table boundaries, not column boundaries. Should be two tables: proposed_claims and runtime_claims with one-way promotion API requiring human review + evidence hash + reviewer identity.
    22	3. Phased plan structure — correct but ordered backwards. Phase 3 (Prove Uplift) comes after 6-10 days of Phase 1-2 build. Popperian order: Phase -1 = hand-write 20 case pages, inject into 10 held-out insurance_risk runs, measure delta. If <15%, stop. Then Phases 0-7.
    23	
    24	## 3. Silent invariants I would add as first-class
    25	### Falsifiability as required field
    26	A claim with provenance but no refutation test is a religious belief. Every claim must carry `falsifier`: "this claim would be refuted if evidence X appeared."
    27	
    28	### Staleness as intrinsic, not retention policy
    29	Every claim class has a confirmation cadence from its physics: architecture/mission baseline 180d, subsystem anomaly pattern 30d, single-analysis interpretation 14d. On lapse, claim auto-demotes from runtime-eligible to proposed. Demotion reversible, deletion destroys audit trail.
    30	
    31	### Adversarial-data defense for public-data lineage
    32	Public-data-derived claims (CelesTrak, SATNOGS, UCS, SpaceTrack, ORDEM lineage) require cross-source corroboration from ≥2 independent sources before runtime eligibility. Single-source claims can be proposed but not promoted.
    33	
    34	## 4. First-principles inversion
    35	Four axioms:
    36	- Information has value only insofar as it changes a decision.
    37	- Every analysis costs tokens × latency × human attention.
    38	- Autonomous writes to runtime-eligible state must be undoable, traceable, rate-limited.
    39	- A claim without a refutation test is not knowledge.
    40	
    41	Entailed architecture:
    42	1. Eval-first. Week 1 = hand-crafted eval harness, 20 insurance_risk analyses, 10 hand-written precedent packs, measured on triage-score delta + analyst-agreement + citation precision.
    43	2. Five-key case page index on (asset, subsystem, failure_family, operator, orbit_regime).
    44	3. Two-table claim lifecycle: proposed_claims + runtime_claims + one-way promotion API.
    45	4. Pure-function crystallizer: crystallize(analysis, evidence, prior_claims) -> case_page deterministic over inputs, regression-testable against frozen snapshots.
    46	5. Cadence-driven demotion.
    47	6. Cross-source corroboration gate for public-data-derived runtime promotion.
    48	7. Backward from the decision, not forward from the data.
    49	
    50	## 5. Comparison with brainstorming/autonomous-intelligence-layer-plan.md
    51	Strictly worse than the memo for this codebase:
    52	- 31 new files, 2,630 LOC, 3 migrations before any eval uplift — violates thin-slice.
    53	- Autoresearch promoting hypotheses into baseline_reference — if any runtime agent reads baseline_reference, autonomous writes bypass fail-closed governance. Load-bearing contradiction.
    54	- A2A messaging + agent harness — coordination complexity before what it coordinates has proven value.
    55	- "Zero risk additive migrations" is misleading when tables encode governance boundaries.
    56	Memo's Phase 0 rule — "if thin slice does not work, the platform should not be built out further" — is the exact principle the brainstorming doc violates.
    57	
    58	## 6. 30-day plan
    59	Days 1-5: Eval harness. 20 precedent packs hand-written. With-vs-without delta. Gate ≥15%.
    60	Days 6-12: proposed_claims + case_pages (five-key indexed) + falsifier + confirmation_cadence columns. Crystallize same 20 analyses. Diff vs hand-written.
    61	Days 13-20: runtime_claims + one-way promotion API + human review + cross-source gate. Wire single injection point in insurance_risk. Magic demo.
    62	Days 21-30: Staleness demoter as background job. Adversarial test: poisoned TLE-derived claim blocked at promotion gate. Drift test: mutate crystallizer LLM temperature, frozen-snapshot regression catches it.
    63	
    64	## Bottom line
    65	Memo's instincts correct on every high-stakes call. What it lacks is the Popperian spine: claim is not knowledge until it carries its own falsifier; build is not justified until value hypothesis has been attacked; autonomous write is not safe until blast radius bounded by cadence and corroboration. Add those three invariants, invert build/measure order, and the architecture lets Orbital Inspect compound in capability without losing the property that makes it sellable to an insurer — that every decision can be taken apart and defended.

     4	# backend
     5	
     6	## Purpose
     7	Python/FastAPI service implementing the 5-agent satellite insurance underwriting pipeline. Owns the LLM orchestration (Gemini), public-data ingestion (TLE / ORDEM / SATNOGS / UCS / SpaceTrack / Space Weather), durable job execution, decision workflow, provenance, and evidence persistence. Exposes REST + SSE to the frontend and PDF/webhook outbound integrations.
     8	
     9	## Key Files
    10	| File | Description |
    11	|------|-------------|
    12	| `main.py` | FastAPI entrypoint — router mounting, middleware, lifespan |
    13	| `config.py` | Pydantic settings (env, secrets, feature flags) |
    14	| `requirements.txt` | Pinned Python dependencies |
    15	| `alembic.ini` | Alembic migration config |
    16	| `pytest.ini` | Pytest markers, paths, coverage config |
    17	| `Dockerfile` | Production container image |
    18	| `orbital_inspect.db` | SQLite dev DB (gitignored in prod workflows) |
    19	
    20	## Subdirectories
    21	| Directory | Purpose |
    22	|-----------|---------|
    23	| `agents/` | 5-agent pipeline + orchestrator (see `agents/AGENTS.md`) |
    24	| `api/` | REST routers (see `api/AGENTS.md`) |
    25	| `auth/` | JWT, RBAC, rate limiting (see `auth/AGENTS.md`) |
    26	| `db/` | SQLAlchemy models + repository (see `db/AGENTS.md`) |
    27	| `middleware/` | Request logging, correlation IDs (see `middleware/AGENTS.md`) |
    28	| `models/` | Pydantic data contracts (see `models/AGENTS.md`) |
    29	| `services/` | ~40 domain services — LLM, public data, telemetry, decisions, resilience (see `services/AGENTS.md`) |
    30	| `workers/` | Durable background workers (see `workers/AGENTS.md`) |
    31	| `scripts/` | Maintenance/codegen scripts — OpenAPI export, type sync, seeds (see `scripts/AGENTS.md`) |
    32	| `tests/` | Pytest suites (see `tests/AGENTS.md`) |
    33	| `alembic/` | Database migrations (see `alembic/AGENTS.md`) |
    34	| `prompts/` | Per-agent LLM prompt templates (see `prompts/AGENTS.md`) |
    35	| `templates/` | Jinja HTML templates (PDF report) — single file |
    36	| `data/` | Runtime storage, demo cache, uploads, ORDEM tables (not documented) |
    37	| `utils/` | Shared utilities (currently minimal) |
    38	
    39	## For AI Agents
    40	
    41	### Working In This Directory
    42	- **Never bypass `resilient_call()`** for agent invocations — it provides timeout, retry, and circuit breaker per Audit Rec #3.
    43	- **Never weaken** the fail-closed classification rejection in the orchestrator.
    44	- **Never** add an agent without registering it in `AGENT_ORDER` in `agents/orchestrator.py`.
    45	- Agent error handlers must return `degraded=True`, never silently succeed.
    46	- Evidence gaps must force `FURTHER_INVESTIGATION` recommendation — do not mask them.
    47	- LLM output handling changes (`services/gemini_service.py`, `parse_json_response`, agent error paths) trigger cross-model review.
    48	
    49	### Testing Requirements
    50	- `cd backend && pytest` runs the full suite.
    51	- Add a unit/integration test under `tests/` for every new service or agent, including the degraded path.
    52	- Offline eval: `pytest tests/test_offline_eval.py` for regression/eval harness (Audit Rec #20).
    53	
    54	### Common Patterns
    55	- `async`/`await` for I/O, `structlog` for logging, Pydantic for all data contracts.
    56	- Repository pattern — business logic in `services/`, SQL isolated in `db/repository.py`.
    57	
    58	## Dependencies
    59	
    60	### Internal
    61	- Frontend consumes generated types from `scripts/generate_types.py` (Audit Rec #9).
    62	
    63	### External
    64	- FastAPI, Uvicorn, SQLAlchemy, Alembic, Pydantic, structlog.
    65	- Redis (queue + rate limit), Postgres (prod) / SQLite (dev).
    66	- Google Gemini via `google-genai` / ADK.

    82	## For AI Agents
    83	
    84	### Working In This Directory
    85	- **Never bypass `resilience.resilient_call()`** for agent/external calls.
    86	- **LLM output handling changes** (`gemini_service.py`) trigger cross-model review.
    87	- Every new service gets: type hints, structlog logger, unit test in `../tests/`, and entry here.

    90	
    91	### Testing Requirements
    92	- Each theme has its test file: `test_gemini_service.py`, `test_public_data_services.py`, `test_resilience.py`, `test_telemetry_services.py`, `test_ordem_service.py`, `test_decision_policy.py`, `test_sensitivity.py`, `test_evidence.py`, `test_storage_service.py`, `test_pdf_report_service.py`, `test_webhook_security.py`, `test_observability.py`, `test_reference_profile_integration.py`.
    93	- Offline eval: `test_offline_eval.py` (Audit Rec #20).
    94	
    95	### Common Patterns
    96	- Async functions, explicit return types, structlog logger at module top.
    97	- Secrets via `secret_service.py`, feature flags via `feature_flag_service.py` — no hardcoded toggles.
    98	
    99	## Dependencies
   100	
   101	### Internal
   102	- `../agents/`, `../api/`, `../db/repository.py`, `../models/`, `../workers/`.
   103	
   104	### External
   105	- google-genai / ADK (Gemini), redis, prometheus_client, opentelemetry, reportlab or weasyprint (PDF), httpx.

 succeeded in 0ms:
     1	<!-- Parent: ../AGENTS.md -->
     2	<!-- Generated: 2026-04-18 | Updated: 2026-04-18 -->
     3	
     4	# agents
     5	
     6	## Purpose
     7	The 5-agent pipeline and its orchestrator. Each agent wraps a Gemini LLM call against its prompt template in `../prompts/`, parses the JSON response, and emits evidence + a stage verdict. The orchestrator enforces `AGENT_ORDER`, fails closed on classification rejection, propagates degraded state, and blocks downstream stages when upstream evidence is missing (Audit Rec #4).
     8	
     9	## Key Files
    10	| File | Description |
    11	|------|-------------|
    12	| `orbital_classification_agent.py` | Stage 1 — classify whether target is a satellite (fail-closed on rejection) |
    13	| `satellite_vision_agent.py` | Stage 2 — vision analysis with bounding-box evidence |
    14	| `orbital_environment_agent.py` | Stage 3 — environment risks (debris, weather, conjunctions) |
    15	| `satellite_failure_mode_agent.py` | Stage 4 — probable failure modes and degradation |
    16	| `insurance_risk_agent.py` | Stage 5 — insurance risk matrix + underwriting recommendation |
    17	| `orchestrator.py` | Pipeline driver — `AGENT_ORDER`, resilient_call, SSE emission, degraded propagation |
    18	| `__init__.py` | Package exports |
    19	
    20	## For AI Agents
    21	
    22	### Working In This Directory
    23	- **Never** add an agent without registering it in `AGENT_ORDER` in `orchestrator.py`.
    24	- Every agent must return `degraded=True` on error — never silently succeed.
    25	- LLM output handling goes through `services/gemini_service.py` (`parse_json_response`); do not parse JSON ad-hoc.
    26	- The classification rejection is fail-closed: if stage 1 rejects, downstream stages must not run.
    27	- Evidence gaps must force `FURTHER_INVESTIGATION` in the final recommendation — do not backfill with defaults.
    28	- Changes here trigger cross-model review (pipeline changes + LLM output handling per `CLAUDE.md`).
    29	
    30	### Testing Requirements
    31	- Add a test in `../tests/` for every new agent covering both happy path and degraded path.
    32	- Consistency contracts live in `test_insurance_consistency.py`; extend there when changing risk logic.
    33	
    34	### Common Patterns
    35	- One agent per file, instantiated at module import, invoked via `resilient_call(agent, ...)`.
    36	- Prompts are loaded from `../prompts/<agent>_prompt.txt` at construction.
    37	
    38	## Dependencies
    39	
    40	### Internal
    41	- `../prompts/` (LLM prompt templates), `../services/gemini_service.py` (LLM client + JSON parsing), `../services/resilience.py` (timeout / retry / circuit breaker), `../models/` (Pydantic contracts for evidence + events).
    42	
    43	<!-- MANUAL: -->

     4	# db
     5	
     6	## Purpose
     7	SQLAlchemy ORM layer — models, engine/session setup, and the repository facade used by services. Postgres in prod, SQLite in dev. All SQL lives here; services must not write raw queries.
     8	
     9	## Key Files
    10	| File | Description |
    11	|------|-------------|
    12	| `base.py` | Declarative base, engine, session factory, lifecycle |
    13	| `models.py` | Core ORM models — analyses, events, outputs, evidence, users, orgs (Audit Rec #5) |
    14	| `batch_models.py` | Batch-job ORM models |
    15	| `repository.py` | Repository facade — all read/write helpers consumed by services |
    16	| `__init__.py` | Package exports |
    17	
    18	## For AI Agents
    19	
    20	### Working In This Directory
    21	- Schema changes trigger cross-model review per `CLAUDE.md`.
    22	- Every schema change needs a matching Alembic migration in `../alembic/versions/`.
    23	- Keep SQL in `repository.py`; services call repository functions, not SQLAlchemy sessions directly.
    24	- Avoid full-table loads in hot paths — prior regression was the asset detail evidence load (see recent commit history).
    25	
    26	### Testing Requirements
    27	- `../tests/test_models.py`, `../tests/test_evidence_repository.py`, `../tests/test_migrations.py` must pass.
    28	
    29	## Dependencies
    30	
    31	### Internal
    32	- `../alembic/` (migrations), `../models/` (Pydantic DTOs that cross the API boundary).
    33	
    34	### External

     1	# Orbital Inspect — Claude Code Instructions
     2	
     3	## Project Context
     4	
     5	Orbital Inspect is a multi-agent satellite insurance underwriting intelligence platform.
     6	5-agent pipeline: Classification -> Vision -> Environment -> Failure Mode -> Insurance Risk.
     7	Backend: Python/FastAPI. Frontend: React/Vite/TypeScript/Tailwind. DB: Postgres (prod), SQLite (dev).
     8	
     9	## Multi-Model Workflow
    10	
    11	This project uses a structured multi-model AI engineering workflow. You (Claude) are the **primary builder**.
    12	
    13	### Your Role: Builder
    14	- Feature implementation, refactoring, bug fixes
    15	- Test writing and CI maintenance
    16	- Documentation and code comments
    17	- Responding to audit findings from other models
    18	
    19	### Other Models in This Project
    20	- **Codex GPT 5.4** (via Codex CLI): Architecture auditor, verifier, targeted feature builds
    21	- **Gemini 3.1 Pro** (via Gemini CLI): Independent validator, cross-check, tie-breaker
    22	
    23	### Attribution Rules (MANDATORY)
    24	
    25	Every commit MUST include `Co-Authored-By` tags for ALL AI models that contributed:
    26	
    27	```
    28	Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.6 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    29	```
    30	
    31	If implementing findings from another model's audit or review, ALSO credit that model in the commit body:
    32	
    33	```
    34	Implements findings from GPT 5.4 architecture audit (AUDIT-GPT54.md, Rec #3).
    35	
    36	Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.6 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    37	```
    38	
    39	Never omit attribution. The git history is the audit trail for the multi-model workflow.
    40	
    41	### Cross-Model Verification Gates
    42	
    43	When making changes in these areas, flag that cross-model review is recommended:
    44	- **Security**: auth, crypto, SSRF prevention, input validation
    45	- **LLM output handling**: gemini_service.py, parse_json_response, agent error paths
    46	- **New agents or pipeline changes**: orchestrator.py, any new agent
    47	- **Insurance risk logic**: risk matrix, underwriting recommendations, provenance
    48	- **Schema changes**: alembic migrations, db/models.py
    49	
    50	### Code Conventions
    51	- Python: async/await, structlog for logging, Pydantic models for all data
    52	- Frontend: TypeScript strict mode, no `any` types, Tailwind for styling
    53	- Tests: pytest (backend), vitest (frontend), playwright (e2e)
    54	- All agent error handlers must return `degraded=True`, never silently succeed
    55	- Evidence gaps must force `FURTHER_INVESTIGATION` recommendation
    56	
    57	### What NOT to Do
    58	- Do not remove or weaken the fail-closed classification rejection
    59	- Do not bypass resilient_call() for agent invocations
    60	- Do not add agents without updating AGENT_ORDER in orchestrator.py
    61	- Do not commit .env files or API keys

/bin/bash -lc "nl -ba ops/architecture/KARPATHY_LLM_WIKI_STRATEGY.md | sed -n '261,520p'" in /mnt/c/Users/kiran/myprojects/orbital-inspect
 succeeded in 0ms:
   261	4. create fleet-level memory across time, subsystems, and operators
   262	
   263	The right conceptual model is:
   264	
   265	- evidence records are the facts and observations
   266	- analyses are the reasoning episodes
   267	- compiled knowledge is the durable memory
   268	- decision workflow is the authority boundary
   269	
   270	## What To Build
   271	
   272	### Karpathy-Style Target Shape
   273	
   274	The right first move is not "build the memory platform."
   275	
   276	The right first move is to prove one compounding loop:
   277	
   278	1. a completed analysis produces an inspectable compiled artifact
   279	2. that artifact is reused in the next similar analysis
   280	3. one agent performs better because it received the right prior context
   281	4. the human can inspect exactly what memory was used and why
   282	
   283	If that loop works, then broader memory infrastructure is justified.
   284	If that loop does not work, then the platform should not be built out further.
   285	
   286	### The Magic Demo
   287	
   288	The plan should optimize for a single obvious demo:
   289	
   290	- analysis A finishes
   291	- Orbital Inspect crystallizes analysis A into a case page plus a small set of candidate claims
   292	- analysis B arrives for a similar asset, subsystem, or anomaly family
   293	- Orbital Inspect builds a compact context pack from that prior case
   294	- one downstream agent uses it
   295	- the analyst can see both the compiled case page and the exact context pack that influenced the new run
   296	
   297	That is the Karpathy-native product test for this repo.
   298	
   299	### Minimal Vertical Slice
   300	
   301	Start with one agent, one memory surface, one retrieval path.
   302	
   303	Recommended first target:
   304	
   305	- agent: `insurance_risk`
   306	- reason: it benefits most directly from precedent, contradiction handling, and reusable synthesized case memory
   307	
   308	The smallest useful loop is:
   309	
   310	- raw evidence and analysis outputs stay as source of truth
   311	- one human-inspectable case page is generated per completed analysis
   312	- a compact precedent context pack is built only for `insurance_risk`
   313	- the result is measured against baseline behavior
   314	
   315	### Target Architecture After the Thin Slice Proves Value
   316	
   317	Add a middle layer between raw evidence and runtime reasoning, but in stages.
   318	
   319	### Layer 1: Raw Evidence and Episodes
   320	
   321	Keep current source of truth unchanged:
   322	
   323	- `evidence_records`
   324	- `analysis_evidence_links`
   325	- `asset_reference_profiles`
   326	- `ingest_runs`
   327	- `analyses`
   328	- `analysis_events`
   329	- `reports`
   330	
   331	### Layer 2: Inspectable Compiled Memory
   332	
   333	This is the first new layer and should be visibly browseable by humans.
   334	
   335	Start with:
   336	
   337	- `knowledge_documents`
   338	  - human-readable case pages, asset dossiers, precedent pages, anomaly summaries
   339	- `knowledge_runs`
   340	  - crystallize, refresh, lint, and context-pack generation runs
   341	- `context_packs`
   342	  - per-agent, per-task snapshots of retrieved memory
   343	
   344	Only add canonical structured claims when the thin slice proves useful:
   345	
   346	- `knowledge_claims`
   347	  - atomic claims with provenance and confidence
   348	
   349	Only add graph-heavy coordination later if needed:
   350	
   351	- `knowledge_edges`
   352	- `knowledge_reviews`
   353	
   354	### Layer 3: Schema and Runtime Policy
   355	
   356	Add a schema document that tells agents how compiled knowledge is created and when it is allowed into runtime context.
   357	
   358	This should define:
   359	
   360	- what qualifies as a case page
   361	- what qualifies as a claim
   362	- which claims are runtime-eligible
   363	- which agent may consume which memory class
   364	- tenant and classification scoping
   365	- human review and supersession rules
   366	- retention and decay policies
   367	
   368	## Proposed Data Model
   369	
   370	### Minimal Start
   371	
   372	The first implementation should resist over-modeling.
   373	
   374	Minimum viable primitives:
   375	
   376	### `knowledge_documents`
   377	
   378	Fields should cover:
   379	
   380	- `id`
   381	- `org_id`
   382	- `asset_id`
   383	- `subsystem_id`
   384	- `document_type`
   385	  - `case_page`, `asset_dossier`, `precedent_page`, `anomaly_summary`
   386	- `title`
   387	- `body_markdown`
   388	- `summary_json`
   389	- `derived_from_analysis_id`
   390	- `classification`
   391	- `status`
   392	  - `generated`, `reviewed`, `approved`, `superseded`
   393	- `created_at`
   394	- `updated_at`
   395	
   396	### `knowledge_runs`
   397	
   398	Fields should cover:
   399	
   400	- `id`
   401	- `org_id`
   402	- `run_type`
   403	  - `crystallize`, `refresh`, `lint`, `build_context_pack`
   404	- `status`
   405	- `source_analysis_id`
   406	- `output_document_id`
   407	- `metrics_json`
   408	- `created_at`
   409	- `completed_at`
   410	
   411	### `context_packs`
   412	
   413	Fields should cover:
   414	
   415	- `id`
   416	- `org_id`
   417	- `analysis_id`
   418	- `agent_name`
   419	- `pack_type`
   420	- `sources_json`
   421	- `content_json`
   422	- `token_estimate`
   423	- `created_at`
   424	
   425	### Expanded Model Once the Loop Works
   426	
   427	Only after the vertical slice proves value should the repo introduce richer canonical structures.
   428	
   429	### `knowledge_claims`
   430	
   431	Expanded fields:
   432	
   433	- `id`
   434	- `org_id`
   435	- `asset_id`
   436	- `subsystem_id`
   437	- `claim_type`
   438	- `claim_text`
   439	- `normalized_payload_json`
   440	- `confidence_score`
   441	- `confidence_basis_json`
   442	- `claim_status`
   443	  - `proposed`, `reviewed`, `approved`, `rejected`, `superseded`
   444	- `supersedes_claim_id`
   445	- `derived_from_analysis_id`
   446	- `last_confirmed_at`
   447	- `last_accessed_at`
   448	- `decay_profile`
   449	- `classification`
   450	- `runtime_eligible`
   451	- `created_at`
   452	- `updated_at`
   453	
   454	### `knowledge_edges`
   455	
   456	Typed relations such as:
   457	
   458	- `supports`
   459	- `contradicts`
   460	- `supersedes`
   461	- `caused`
   462	- `similar_to`
   463	- `same_failure_family`
   464	- `affects_subsystem`
   465	- `precedent_for`
   466	- `mitigated_by`
   467	- `derived_from`
   468	
   469	## How This Helps Orbital Inspect Specifically
   470	
   471	### 1. Better per-analysis context packs
   472	
   473	Today the system can fetch relevant evidence. With compiled knowledge it can also inject:
   474	
   475	- prior anomaly families on the same subsystem
   476	- similar cases from the same orbit regime
   477	- known contradictions for this asset baseline
   478	- operator-specific maintenance and trend patterns
   479	- historically effective mitigation actions
   480	
   481	This raises quality without requiring the agents to rediscover patterns from scratch.
   482	
   483	### 2. Faster human review
   484	
   485	Human review should not open a case from zero. It should open with:
   486	
   487	- current risk summary
   488	- top supporting evidence
   489	- top contradicting evidence
   490	- nearest historical precedents
   491	- what changed since last review
   492	- why the decision policy landed where it did
   493	
   494	That is a direct application of Karpathy's "compiled knowledge" idea to underwriting operations.
   495	
   496	### 3. Fleet memory instead of only fleet metrics
   497	
   498	The current trend and portfolio surfaces tell you what is happening.
   499	The compiled layer can tell you what kind of thing keeps happening.
   500	
   501	That means:
   502	
   503	- recurring failure families
   504	- subsystem clusters with similar degradation signatures
   505	- operators with repeated evidence gaps
   506	- orbits and environmental conditions associated with escalations
   507	
   508	### 4. Better prompt and policy iteration
   509	
   510	Compiled memory should not only be about satellites. It should also capture:
   511	
   512	- prompt failures
   513	- parsing failures
   514	- recurring evidence gaps
   515	- false confidence patterns
   516	- benchmark misses
   517	
   518	That becomes a self-improving loop for the product.
   519	
   520	## What Not To Do

exec

     3	
     4	Tables:
     5	  - organizations: Multi-tenant org records
     6	  - assets: Stable orbital asset identities within an org
     7	  - asset_aliases: Canonical and external identifiers for assets
     8	  - asset_subsystems: Stable subsystem identities within an asset
     9	  - asset_reference_profiles: Canonical baseline/reference profiles for assets

/bin/bash -lc "nl -ba backend/models/provenance.py | sed -n '1,260p'" in /mnt/c/Users/kiran/myprojects/orbital-inspect
 succeeded in 0ms:
     1	"""
     2	Data provenance, confidence calibration, and sensitivity analysis models.
     3	
     4	Implements David Deutsch's 'hard to vary' principle — every number must be
     5	traceable to its source, every confidence calibrated, every probability derived.
     6	"""
     7	
     8	from pydantic import BaseModel
     9	from enum import Enum
    10	
    11	
    12	class DataSourceType(str, Enum):
    13	    MEASURED = "measured"
    14	    INFERRED = "inferred"
    15	    ESTIMATED = "estimated"
    16	    REFERENCE = "reference"
    17	    OPERATOR_REPORTED = "reported"
    18	
    19	
    20	class FieldProvenance(BaseModel):
    21	    source_type: DataSourceType = DataSourceType.ESTIMATED
    22	    primary_source: str = ""
    23	    confidence: float = 0.5
    24	    derivation_chain: list[str] = []
    25	    caveats: list[str] = []
    26	
    27	
    28	class ConfidenceCalibration(BaseModel):
    29	    evidence_sufficiency: float = 0.5
    30	    model_uncertainty: float = 0.5
    31	    consensus_strength: float = 0.5
    32	    calibrated_confidence: float = 0.5
    33	    confidence_tier: str = "MODERATE"
    34	    basis: str = ""
    35	
    36	
    37	class FinancialEstimate(BaseModel):
    38	    value_usd: float = 0
    39	    source: str = ""
    40	    confidence_range_low: float = 0
    41	    confidence_range_high: float = 0
    42	    comparable_precedents: list[str] = []
    43	    derivation: str = ""
    44	
    45	
    46	class ProbabilityComponent(BaseModel):
    47	    mechanism: str = ""
    48	    base_rate: float = 0
    49	    observed_evidence_factor: float = 1.0
    50	    adjusted_probability: float = 0
    51	    source: str = ""
    52	
    53	
    54	class LossProbabilityDerivation(BaseModel):
    55	    components: list[ProbabilityComponent] = []
    56	    aggregation_method: str = "independent_sum"
    57	    total_loss_probability: float = 0
    58	    derivation_narrative: str = ""
    59	
    60	
    61	class SensitivityParameter(BaseModel):
    62	    name: str = ""
    63	    baseline_value: float = 0
    64	    test_range_low: float = 0
    65	    test_range_high: float = 0
    66	    recommendation_at_low: str = ""
    67	    recommendation_at_high: str = ""
    68	    is_critical: bool = False
    69	
    70	
    71	class SensitivityAnalysis(BaseModel):
    72	    parameters: list[SensitivityParameter] = []
    73	    baseline_recommendation: str = ""
    74	    recommendation_robustness: str = "MODERATE"
    75	    critical_thresholds: list[str] = []
    76	    key_drivers: list[str] = []

 succeeded in 0ms:
     1	"""
     2	Gemini + ADK service layer for Orbital Inspect.
     3	
     4	Provides ADK-native agent execution with raw Gemini fallback.
     5	Inherited from DeepInspect, adapted for satellite inspection domain.
     6	"""
     7	
     8	import json
     9	import uuid
    10	import asyncio
    11	import logging
    12	import os
    13	from config import settings
    14	
    15	log = logging.getLogger(__name__)
    16	
    17	if settings.GEMINI_API_KEY:
    18	    os.environ.setdefault("GEMINI_API_KEY", settings.GEMINI_API_KEY)
    19	    os.environ.setdefault("GOOGLE_API_KEY", settings.GEMINI_API_KEY)
    20	
    21	_ADK_AVAILABLE = False
    22	
    23	try:
    24	    from google.adk.agents import Agent, ParallelAgent
    25	    from google.adk.runners import Runner
    26	    from google.adk.sessions import InMemorySessionService
    27	    from google.adk.tools import google_search
    28	    from google import genai
    29	    from google.genai import types
    30	
    31	    client = genai.Client(api_key=settings.GEMINI_API_KEY)
    32	    _ADK_AVAILABLE = True
    33	    log.info("Google ADK loaded successfully")
    34	except ImportError as e:
    35	    log.warning("ADK not available, using raw Gemini fallback", extra={"error": str(e)})
    36	    try:
    37	        from google import genai
    38	        from google.genai import types
    39	        client = genai.Client(api_key=settings.GEMINI_API_KEY)
    40	    except ImportError:
    41	        client = None
    42	
    43	APP_NAME = "orbital_inspect"
    44	
    45	if _ADK_AVAILABLE:
    46	    _session_service = InMemorySessionService()
    47	else:
    48	    _session_service = None
    49	
    50	
    51	def is_adk_available() -> bool:
    52	    return _ADK_AVAILABLE
    53	
    54	
    55	def get_model_name() -> str:
    56	    return settings.GEMINI_MODEL
    57	
    58	
    59	async def run_adk_agent(
    60	    agent: "Agent",
    61	    user_message: str,
    62	    image_bytes: bytes | None = None,
    63	    image_mime: str = "image/jpeg",
    64	    session_state: dict | None = None,
    65	) -> dict:
    66	    """Execute an ADK agent and return parsed JSON response."""
    67	    if not _ADK_AVAILABLE:
    68	        return await _run_fallback(agent, user_message, image_bytes, image_mime)
    69	
    70	    user_id = f"user_{uuid.uuid4().hex[:8]}"
    71	    session = await _session_service.create_session(
    72	        app_name=APP_NAME,
    73	        user_id=user_id,
    74	        state=session_state or {},
    75	    )
    76	
    77	    parts = [types.Part.from_text(text=user_message)]
    78	    if image_bytes:
    79	        parts.append(types.Part.from_bytes(data=image_bytes, mime_type=image_mime))
    80	
    81	    message = types.Content(role="user", parts=parts)
    82	
    83	    final_text = ""
    84	    runner = Runner(
    85	        agent=agent,
    86	        app_name=APP_NAME,
    87	        session_service=_session_service,
    88	    )
    89	
    90	    async for event in runner.run_async(
    91	        user_id=user_id,
    92	        session_id=session.id,
    93	        new_message=message,
    94	    ):
    95	        if event.is_final_response():
    96	            if event.content and event.content.parts:
    97	                for part in event.content.parts:
    98	                    if part.text:
    99	                        final_text += part.text
   100	
   101	    return parse_json_response(final_text)
   102	
   103	
   104	def parse_json_response(text: str) -> dict:
   105	    """Extract JSON from agent response, handling markdown code fences."""
   106	    text = text.strip()
   107	    if text.startswith("```"):
   108	        lines = text.split("\n")
   109	        lines = [l for l in lines if not l.strip().startswith("```")]
   110	        text = "\n".join(lines).strip()
   111	    try:
   112	        return json.loads(text)
   113	    except json.JSONDecodeError:
   114	        start = text.find("{")
   115	        end = text.rfind("}") + 1
   116	        if start >= 0 and end > start:
   117	            try:
   118	                return json.loads(text[start:end])
   119	            except json.JSONDecodeError:
   120	                pass
   121	        return {"error": "Failed to parse agent response", "raw_text": text[:500]}
   122	
   123	
   124	async def _run_fallback(
   125	    agent: object,
   126	    user_message: str,
   127	    image_bytes: bytes | None = None,
   128	    image_mime: str = "image/jpeg",
   129	) -> dict:
   130	    """Fallback using raw google-genai Client. Uses run_in_executor to avoid blocking."""
   131	    instruction = getattr(agent, "instruction", "") or ""
   132	    model_name = getattr(agent, "model", settings.GEMINI_MODEL) or settings.GEMINI_MODEL
   133	
   134	    if client is None:
   135	        raise RuntimeError("No Gemini client available")
   136	
   137	    contents_parts = []
   138	    if instruction:
   139	        contents_parts.append(types.Part.from_text(text=instruction))
   140	    contents_parts.append(types.Part.from_text(text=user_message))
   141	
   142	    if image_bytes:
   143	        contents_parts.append(types.Part.from_bytes(data=image_bytes, mime_type=image_mime))
   144	
   145	    def _sync_call():
   146	        return client.models.generate_content(
   147	            model=model_name,
   148	            contents=types.Content(role="user", parts=contents_parts),
   149	            config=types.GenerateContentConfig(
   150	                response_mime_type="application/json",
   151	                temperature=0.1,
   152	            ),
   153	        )
   154	
   155	    loop = asyncio.get_running_loop()
   156	    response = await loop.run_in_executor(None, _sync_call)
   157	    return parse_json_response(response.text or "")

    14	ACTION_TYPES = {

    16	    "monitor",

    22	}
    23	DECISION_STATUSES = {"pending_policy", "pending_human_review", "approved_for_use", "blocked"}
    24	URGENCY_SCORES = {"routine": 0.2, "priority": 0.65, "urgent": 1.0}
    25	TRIAGE_BANDS = (
    26	    (0.80, "urgent"),
    27	    (0.60, "priority"),
    28	    (0.35, "elevated"),
    29	    (0.00, "routine"),

    34	class DecisionOutcome:

    39	def _clamp(value: float, low: float, high: float) -> float:
    40	    return max(low, min(high, value))
    41	
    42	
    43	def _coerce_utc(dt: datetime | None) -> datetime | None:
    44	    if dt is None:
    45	        return None
    46	    if dt.tzinfo is None or dt.tzinfo.utcoffset(dt) is None:
    47	        return dt.replace(tzinfo=timezone.utc)
    48	    return dt.astimezone(timezone.utc)

    51	def _evidence_bucket(evidence_completeness_pct: float | None) -> str:
    52	    if evidence_completeness_pct is None:
    53	        return "insufficient"
    54	    if evidence_completeness_pct >= 85:
    55	        return "sufficient"
    56	    if evidence_completeness_pct >= 60:
    57	        return "partial"
    58	    return "insufficient"

    61	def _parse_composite(insurance_result: dict[str, Any]) -> int:
    62	    risk_matrix = insurance_result.get("risk_matrix") or {}
    63	    composite = risk_matrix.get("composite")
    64	    try:
    65	        return max(0, min(125, int(composite)))
    66	    except (TypeError, ValueError):
    67	        return 0
    68	
    69	
    70	def _needs_maneuver_review(environment_result: dict[str, Any] | None, composite: int) -> bool:
    71	    if composite < 90 or not environment_result:
    72	        return False
    73	    collision_probability = str(environment_result.get("collision_probability") or "").lower()
    74	    if collision_probability and any(token in collision_probability for token in ("high", "elevated", "critical")):
    75	        return True
    76	    for stressor in environment_result.get("stressors") or []:
    77	        if not isinstance(stressor, dict):
    78	            continue
    79	        name = str(stressor.get("name") or "").lower()
    80	        severity = str(stressor.get("severity") or "").upper()
    81	        if severity == "HIGH" and any(token in name for token in ("debris", "collision", "conjunction")):
    82	            return True
    83	    return False

    86	def evaluate_decision_policy(analysis) -> DecisionOutcome:
    87	    insurance_result = dict(getattr(analysis, "insurance_risk_result", {}) or {})
    88	    environment_result = dict(getattr(analysis, "environment_result", {}) or {})
    89	    evidence_completeness_pct = getattr(analysis, "evidence_completeness_pct", None)
    90	    evidence_bucket = _evidence_bucket(evidence_completeness_pct)
    91	    degraded = bool(getattr(analysis, "degraded", False))
    92	    failure_reasons = list(getattr(analysis, "failure_reasons", []) or [])
    93	    evidence_gaps = list(insurance_result.get("evidence_gaps") or getattr(analysis, "evidence_gaps", []) or [])
    94	    human_review_required = bool(getattr(analysis, "human_review_required", True))
    95	    status = getattr(analysis, "status", "failed")
    96	    asset_type = getattr(analysis, "asset_type", "satellite")
    97	    composite = _parse_composite(insurance_result)
    98	    risk_tier = str(insurance_result.get("risk_tier") or "UNKNOWN")
    99	    underwriting = str(insurance_result.get("underwriting_recommendation") or "FURTHER_INVESTIGATION")
   100	
   101	    blocked_reason = None
   102	    recommended_action: str | None = None
   103	    decision_confidence = "low"
   104	
   105	    if status == "failed":
   106	        blocked_reason = "analysis failed before a trustworthy operational decision could be produced"
   107	    elif status == "rejected":
   108	        blocked_reason = "target rejected as unsupported or non-orbital imagery"
   109	    elif not insurance_result:
   110	        blocked_reason = "risk synthesis unavailable"
   111	
   112	    if blocked_reason:
   113	        urgency = "priority"
   114	        summary = {
   115	            "recommended_action": None,
   116	            "decision_confidence": "low",
   117	            "decision_rationale": blocked_reason,
   118	            "required_human_review": True,
   119	            "blocked": True,
   120	            "blocked_reason": blocked_reason,
   121	            "evidence_completeness_bucket": evidence_bucket,
   122	            "urgency": urgency,
   123	            "policy_version": settings.GOVERNANCE_POLICY_VERSION,
   124	        }
   125	        return DecisionOutcome(summary=summary, status="blocked")
   126	
   127	    if evidence_bucket == "insufficient" or degraded or getattr(analysis, "report_completeness", "COMPLETE") == "PARTIAL":
   128	        recommended_action = "reimage" if evidence_bucket == "insufficient" or evidence_gaps or failure_reasons else "monitor"
   129	        urgency = "priority" if composite >= 60 else "routine"
   130	        decision_confidence = "low"
   131	        rationale = "Evidence quality is not sufficient for stronger operational use."
   132	        if evidence_gaps:
   133	            rationale += f" Missing or degraded stages: {', '.join(evidence_gaps)}."
   134	        if failure_reasons:
   135	            rationale += " Pipeline recorded failure reasons."
   136	    else:
   137	        if _needs_maneuver_review(environment_result, composite):
   138	            recommended_action = "maneuver_review"
   139	        elif underwriting == "UNINSURABLE":
   140	            recommended_action = "disposal_review" if composite >= 100 else "insurance_escalation"
   141	        elif underwriting == "INSURABLE_WITH_EXCLUSIONS":
   142	            recommended_action = (
   143	                "servicing_candidate"
   144	                if asset_type in {"servicer", "station_module", "solar_array", "radiator", "power_node", "compute_platform"}
   145	                else "insurance_escalation"
   146	            )
   147	        elif underwriting == "INSURABLE_ELEVATED_PREMIUM":
   148	            recommended_action = "insurance_escalation"
   149	        elif underwriting == "FURTHER_INVESTIGATION":
   150	            recommended_action = "monitor"
   151	        elif composite >= 80:
   152	            recommended_action = "insurance_escalation"
   153	        elif composite >= 60:
   154	            recommended_action = "monitor"
   155	        else:
   156	            recommended_action = "continue_operations"
   157	
   158	        urgency = (
   159	            "urgent"
   160	            if recommended_action in {"maneuver_review", "disposal_review"} or composite >= 90
   161	            else "priority"
   162	            if recommended_action in {"reimage", "insurance_escalation", "servicing_candidate"} or composite >= 60
   163	            else "routine"
   164	        )
   165	        decision_confidence = "high" if evidence_bucket == "sufficient" and composite < 60 else "medium"
   166	        rationale = (
   167	            f"Policy mapped {underwriting} at composite {composite}/125 with {risk_tier} risk "
   168	            f"to {recommended_action.replace('_', ' ')}."
   169	        )
   170	
   171	    decision_status = "pending_human_review" if human_review_required else "approved_for_use"
   172	    summary = {
   173	        "recommended_action": recommended_action,
   174	        "decision_confidence": decision_confidence,
   175	        "decision_rationale": rationale,
   176	        "required_human_review": human_review_required,
   177	        "blocked": False,
   178	        "blocked_reason": None,
   179	        "evidence_completeness_bucket": evidence_bucket,
   180	        "urgency": urgency,
   181	        "policy_version": settings.GOVERNANCE_POLICY_VERSION,
   182	    }
   183	    return DecisionOutcome(summary=summary, status=decision_status)
   184	
   185	
   186	def compute_triage(
   187	    analysis,
   188	    *,
   189	    decision_summary: dict[str, Any],
   190	    decision_status: str,
   191	    recurrence_count: int,
   192	    as_of: datetime | None = None,
   193	) -> tuple[float, str, dict[str, float | int | str]]:
   194	    as_of = _coerce_utc(as_of or datetime.now(timezone.utc)) or datetime.now(timezone.utc)
   195	    insurance_result = dict(getattr(analysis, "insurance_risk_result", {}) or {})
   196	    composite = _parse_composite(insurance_result)
   197	    evidence_pct = getattr(analysis, "evidence_completeness_pct", None)
   198	    completed_at = _coerce_utc(
   199	        getattr(analysis, "completed_at", None) or getattr(analysis, "created_at", None)
   200	    )
   201	    age_days = 0.0
   202	    if completed_at is not None:
   203	        age_days = max((as_of - completed_at).total_seconds() / 86400.0, 0.0)
   204	
   205	    normalized_risk = _clamp(composite / 125.0, 0.0, 1.0)
   206	    urgency = str(decision_summary.get("urgency") or "routine")
   207	    urgency_score = URGENCY_SCORES.get(urgency, URGENCY_SCORES["routine"])
   208	    evidence_penalty = 1.0 if evidence_pct is None else 1.0 - _clamp(float(evidence_pct) / 100.0, 0.0, 1.0)
   209	    staleness_score = _clamp(age_days / 90.0, 0.0, 1.0)
   210	    recurrence_score = _clamp(recurrence_count / 3.0, 0.0, 1.0)
   211	    blocked_or_pending_score = 1.0 if decision_status in {"pending_human_review", "blocked"} else 0.0
   212	
   213	    triage_score = round(
   214	        (
   215	            0.35 * normalized_risk
   216	            + 0.25 * urgency_score
   217	            + 0.15 * evidence_penalty
   218	            + 0.10 * staleness_score
   219	            + 0.10 * recurrence_score
   220	            + 0.05 * blocked_or_pending_score
   221	        ),
   222	        4,
   223	    )
   224	
   225	    triage_band = "routine"
   226	    for threshold, band in TRIAGE_BANDS:
   227	        if triage_score >= threshold:
   228	            triage_band = band
   229	            break
   230	
   231	    factors = {
   232	        "normalized_risk": round(normalized_risk, 4),
   233	        "urgency_score": round(urgency_score, 4),
   234	        "evidence_penalty": round(evidence_penalty, 4),
   235	        "staleness_score": round(staleness_score, 4),
   236	        "recurrence_score": round(recurrence_score, 4),
   237	        "blocked_or_pending_score": round(blocked_or_pending_score, 4),
   238	        "age_days": round(age_days, 2),
   239	        "recurrence_count": recurrence_count,
   240	    }
   241	    return triage_score, triage_band, factors

    20	def _clean_text(value: Any) -> str | None:
    21	    if value is None:
    22	        return None
    23	    cleaned = str(value).strip()
    24	    return cleaned or None

    27	def _first_non_empty(*values: Any) -> str | None:
    28	    for value in values:
    29	        cleaned = _clean_text(value)
    30	        if cleaned:
    31	            return cleaned
    32	    return None

    34	
    35	def _coerce_datetime(value: Any) -> datetime | None:
    36	    if value is None:
    37	        return None
    38	    if isinstance(value, datetime):
    39	        if value.tzinfo is None or value.tzinfo.utcoffset(value) is None:
    40	            return value.replace(tzinfo=timezone.utc)
    41	        return value.astimezone(timezone.utc)
    42	    if isinstance(value, str):
    43	        normalized = value.replace("Z", "+00:00")
    44	        try:
    45	            parsed = datetime.fromisoformat(normalized)
    46	        except ValueError:
    47	            return None
    48	        if parsed.tzinfo is None or parsed.tzinfo.utcoffset(parsed) is None:
    49	            return parsed.replace(tzinfo=timezone.utc)
    50	        return parsed.astimezone(timezone.utc)
    51	    return None

    54	def _seed_reference_sources(baseline_reference: dict[str, Any]) -> list[str]:
    55	    raw = baseline_reference.get("reference_sources_json") or baseline_reference.get("reference_sources") or []
    56	    if isinstance(raw, str):
    57	        raw = [raw]
    58	    return [str(item).strip() for item in raw if str(item).strip()]

    60	
    61	def _dedupe_strings(values: list[str]) -> list[str]:
    62	    seen: set[str] = set()
    63	    ordered: list[str] = []
    64	    for value in values:
    65	        cleaned = value.strip()
    66	        if not cleaned or cleaned in seen:
    67	            continue
    68	        seen.add(cleaned)
    69	        ordered.append(cleaned)
    70	    return ordered

    73	def _merge_dimensions(target: dict[str, Any], payload: dict[str, Any]) -> dict[str, Any]:
    74	    keys = (
    75	        "longitude_geo_deg",
    76	        "perigee_km",
    77	        "apogee_km",
    78	        "inclination_deg",
    79	        "period_min",

    85	        "launch_vehicle",
    86	        "launch_site",
    87	        "country_code",
    88	        "object_type",
    89	        "site",
    90	        "status",
    91	    )
    92	    for key in keys:
    93	        value = payload.get(key)
    94	        if value not in (None, "", [], {}):
    95	            target.setdefault(key, value)
    96	    return target
